07/12/2023, 12:15 - Tariq Bin Bashar: The natural order hypothesis is one of the five hypotheses of the monitor model, a theory of second language acquisition proposed by Stephen Krashen. The main point of this hypothesis is that language learners acquire grammatical structures in a predictable and natural order, regardless of their native language, age, or instruction. The order is determined by the complexity and frequency of the structures in the input. For example, learners tend to acquire the plural -s before the past tense -ed, or the present progressive -ing before the third person singular -s. The natural order hypothesis suggests that language acquisition is a natural and innate process that follows a universal pattern.
